commit e81ea035ab3af8a3fc8e231dc0f86fb50eb59d02
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-12-25 05:54:56 +0100

conservative performance optimizations to the keyboard navigation feature
As chatgpt 5.2 explains below (check if accurate, claude opus 4.5 review the change ok and excellent according to it):

That said: the only meaningful O(n) cost you still have with arrows is in SAS_navigateItemList(), because it re-scans self.list on every Up/Down press to rebuild the selectable indices + find current position. On a 2015 CPU this is already fine (lists are usually a few hundred entries), but if you want a safe + reliable micro-optimization, this one is good:

Safe optimization: cache “selectable rows” during placeItems()
What it changes

	- While placeItems() is already looping to draw the table, also build:
		- self.SAS_selectableListIdx: list indices of displayed real items (skips headers/spacers)
		- self.SAS_itemToSelectablePos: maps iItem → position in SAS_selectableListIdx
	- Then SAS_navigateItemList() becomes O(1) per arrow press (no list scanning), while preserving behavior with filtering/headers because the cache is built after filtering rules are applied.

Is this worth it?

	- Correctness risk: low (it’s just caching what you already displayed).
	- Speed gain: small but real (Up/Down becomes constant-time).
	- Compatibility: Python 2.4-safe (no ternaries/comprehensions; I used has_key in the fallback to match old Py2 style, but you can keep idx not in dict if you prefer).

commit ee22ac967d547f3d19888bf90dc0e2c414fbb4d6
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-12-24 16:28:49 +0100

disable events as default in base new game mode ("play now")
- The standard new game mode (**Play Now**) now has **Events Disabled** by default. We find they can be annoying, distracting, or frustrating; they do not bring a real gameplay value to make up for that, and setting up a Custom Game every time to disable them is tedious. Players can still enable events via the **Custom Game** mode: make sure the "No Random Events" option is unticked, or alternatively revert this change. Change in [CIV4GameOptionInfos.xml](/Assets/XML/GameInfo/CIV4GameOptionInfos.xml) (`GAMEOPTION_NO_EVENTS`'s `bDefault`: `0` -> `1`).

commit b5ecf7a37ae7330c65384a4f880d20d344193230
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-12-23 05:51:49 +0100

replace hardcoded CvUnitAI::getBonusSpecificLandBuilds, replaced with dynamic fetch
- replace hardcoded CvUnitAI::getBonusSpecificLandBuilds leads to much more cities at turn 100 and much faster tech pace, and stronger military. Much higher score for all players as well in score board at turn 100 vs turn 200, reproducible too.

e.g. test 1 noble pangea large map:
	- t100: before: scores from 267 (top) to 199 (bottom) -> after: 387 to 265
	- t200: before: scores from 721 (top) to 281 (bottom) -> after: 1140 to 414

e.g. test 2 monarch pangea large map, swap autoplay order, same results:
	- t100: before: scores from 380 (top) to 225 (bottom) -> after: 452 to 240
	- t200: before: scores from 1168 (top) to 667 (bottom) -> after: 1211 to 628

Cause of these results is most likely fixing a bug in a recent CvUnitAI::getBonusSpecificLandBuilds rework that moved them to xml hardcoded defines in an incomplete way, now they are automatically fetched by the DLL without needing XML defines which should be cleaner and more reliable.

See screenshots comparison for before/after changes at: https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advciv-sas-simple-advanced-strategy.699716/post-16901074

- increase tech costs to match this AI strength increase (else they tech too fast):
875->950
1150->1250
1700->1750
1900->1950
2050->2075

commit f8f9ef6d2ce1aec0d27190c6fb68f09bf94adec6

handle duplicates more cleanly and show them in headers in sevopedia bonus's entries grouping
- also bonus naming fix in CIV4PlotLSystem.xml although i am not sure our mod even uses this file, adding just in case to apply our changes there as well.

- about the logic change.:
	# Group bonuses by the improvement(s) that connect them:
	#   Farm -> Corn/Wheat/...
	#   Pasture -> Sheep/Horse/...
	# For multi-improvement bonuses (e.g. Oil: Well + Offshore Platform), we use a combined header.
	# <!-- custom: we did this change because RFC DOC used another water/land tie breaker logic that would display Oil only under "Well", but the player needs to know too that "Offshore Platform" is another improvement trades for Oil. Also, if some mod mod added another improvement trades on land (e.g. Farm + Pasture for Milk (imaginary example)) then the water/land tie breaking would not be effective as well, and we'd miss the info that both improvements support this. This is the only case in our mod (Oil) that has more than one improvement trades., so we don't need to complicate the logic further, while hopefully providing this logic in a bit cleaner or more relevant way to us than in RFC DOC mod (although their code helps lot and with chatgpt 5.2's help too and my help too xd i mean thanks to them and me xd as well) -->

commit fc1bcdb31c3a0329a329f11d9820ca00edf13231

executives now require the same tech(s) as their corresponding corporation building
- **Executives** now **require the same Tech(s)** to be built as their corresponding corporation's does (e.g. `TECH_MARINE_TECHNOLOGY` and `TECH_CORPORATION` for the Sid Sushi's executive unit; was `NONE`.) to be built. This simplifies the Sevopedia Unit Era grouping implementation so they are correctly listed (e.g. "at Modern Era", not at "No Technology Prequisite"), and executive's effective availability (i.e. not until the later eras). This also balances **rival city acquisition** so a player **cannot produce executives if we do not have the corresponding Corporation** in the city (mirroring the shrine prerequirement change).
- add sevopedia unit era grouping

commit c28e40dd39782f69ee82b9b61454ccf21595dc98
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-12-17 15:14:04 +0100

(Fixed) exclude iXMLCost <= 0 buildings from the SAS CvCityAI::AI_buildingValue gates entirely
- Does **not** affect Buildings with a **negative or equal to 0 XML `iCost` (Shrines, Corporations, etc.)**, since we don't need to save hammer for free of cost buildings, and they would otherwise not be built or heavily delayed if affected by any SAS `CvCityAI::AI_buildingValue` gate.

commit 8a13288983ec3e985d67645a803c0f742aa3992a
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-12-17 13:53:23 +0100

(Tremendously Improved) Build very cheap World Wonders ASAP; (Tremendously Improved) Do not Build Barbarian Blocking Wonders past classical era
- Do not build **Anti-Barbarian Border Blocking** (`bBorderObstacle`) **Wonders** (e.g. Great Wall) past a certain **era** (e.g. Classical era, meaning we will not build Great Wall or equivalent wonders from the Medieval and onwards). Change in `CvCityAI::AI_buildingValue`.
- Regardless of the aforementionned pre-filtering rules, **cheap World Wonders ASAP** (hammer `iCost` tunable by era in SAS defines). This is because we have prioritized most early hammer towards early urgent growth (settlers, workers, etc.) or military (urgent rush or defense), and the very cheap cost (e.g. Pyramids not yet built Medieval era) make it attractive and worth having ~1-2 less units or similar. Change in `CvCityAI::AI_buildingValue`. Note: about Wonders generally, AdvCiv-SAS uses a quite strict low wonder policy, as early settlers and workers are more valuable generally and a stronger choice; plus later on we have little time to build world wonders as we risk being overrun by our rivals and building world wonders for them as they conquer us, which is a poor choice. A mostly Base AdvCiv-like behaviour of AIs building many wonders can be restored in SAS defines by disabling `SAS_AI_BUILDING_VALUE_WORLD_WONDERS_OPTIMIZE` (e.g. 0 vs 6 wonders at turn 100 in an autoplay sample with vs without it).

Further addresses: https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advciv-sas-simple-advanced-strategy.699716/post-16898915

- BUILDINGCLASS_ORACLE: change ObsoleteTech from NONE to TECH_BROADER_EDUCATION "<!-- custom: was NONE: now kind of like in civ3 but broader (no pun): this change makes sense i think as older religions eventually start to fade away; plus it allows not to have ridiculously cheap free tech later in the game if not yet build -->"
- BUILDINGCLASS_SHWEDAGON_PAYA: fix incorrect iCost: too high for its column: 375->300 (and then also adjusted as below)

- BUILDINGCLASS_THREE_GORGES_DAM and BUILDINGCLASS_MT_RUSHMORE and BUILDINGCLASS_ROCKNROLL: fix iCost: too low for its column: 650->675 (and then also adjust as below)
- BUILDINGCLASS_APOSTOLIC_PALACE: reduce iCost from 325 to 300: "<!-- custom: make cost quite low as it is more of a shared wonder between all players and we want it in more games than not in them."

wonder costs were too expensive especially early relative to unit/building costs (generally i try to aim for 3x-4x more or less (not necessarily always so always)) and advciv-sas's low modifier from bonuses change.

175->150
200->175
225->200
250->225
300->275
375->350
425->400
500->450
525->475
550->500
575->525
600->550
625->575
650->600
675->625
700->650

They should naturally become more attractive as they are cheaper. We don't want to change the core logic of them not valuing wonders if they are too expensive, as it is a bad move to build them anyway i think.

Is what i thought originally, but upon considering it more, and by disabling SAS_AI_BUILDING_VALUE_WONDERS_OPTIMIZE, now AIs suddenly build a lot of wonders (0 vs 6 wonders at turn 100). It is not necessarily weaker with all the war cheks and min hammer requirements we have. Also it may help them scale better into the late game, as they still have decent military it seems.

"<!-- custom: update: in autoplay, the SAS_AI_BUILDING_VALUE_WORLD_WONDERS_OPTIMIZE check specifically greatly reduces the number of early wonders (0 wonders vs 6 wonders at turn 100 with vs without it, everything else being the same). Tune below sub-kobs if you want more precision, or to restore a more base advciv like behaviour of wonder building, disable SAS_AI_BUILDING_VALUE_WORLD_WONDERS_OPTIMIZE entirely. I believe building settlers or workers is generally stronger especially early, so i kept the "optimize" flag enabled. But you can disable it if you want a more wonder-building like behaviour, or maybe rather one of the sub-knobs as you prefer (but it can quickly become a rabbit hole xd so beware i mean.). See below to specifically tune its suboptions rather. Code added with the help of chatgpt 5.2 thanks -->"

In a bit more detail, we don't want to overdo the wonder cost correction, as wonders are not a shopping list of things that must always be built every game in advciv-sas, only options to choose from or not if deemed relevant (fine to ignore many if not a strong move to build them).

But also, considering it more, even if they are a bit too cheap or may be so, there is still a risk of falling behind militarily and being conquered and so ending up just wasting time and building them for our opponent when they conquer us; with that in mind, it would be fine as such, as unit spam is attractive and reliable, but hopefully wonder building is more so and a more valid strategic option/alternative.

If sas human players disble the xml flag, AIs build wonders seemingly normally and players can adjust it as they prefer).

Adresses: https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advciv-sas-simple-advanced-strategy.699716/post-16898915

tech tree adjustments and enhancements with the help of gemini 3 pro thanks.
- TECH_THE_WHEEL: TECH_ANIMAL_HUSBANDRY AND TECH_MASONRY to the TECH_ANIMAL_HUSBANDRY AND TECH_POTTERY (thematically more correct ("Potter's Wheel" as i had intended then but somehow made stricter for balanced. and less rigid tree, buffs chariots a bit as a side effect since they are available sooner). Additionally allows roads to appear sooner which is much more versatile strategically so better as such i think. Also, ingame it seems that since we unlock roads at the same time to most times link our horse (unless river connectde but most often not), plus the fact that our production capacity is still fairly low so early and longbows not much later and going miltiary would delay our early expansion, this is probably balanced as such. (note: as of now TECH_CONSTRUCTION still requires TECH_MASONRY as thematically more correct and most importantly for balance)
- TECH_BRONZE_WORKING: remove the TECH_AGRICULTURE (now only requires TECH_METAL_CASTING): thematically more correct, and more importantly for balance we get bronze working way too late still. Even though it requires less techs than the wheel for chariots, it is in a higher tier so fine as such. Plus, it is significantly riskier, as bronze working does not leads to as many techs, plus is not tradeable in our mod, so fine to relax the requirement there. This rewards such a risk more as well. Gemini 3 pro also advises changing it as such thanks.
- TECH_DRAMA: remove the TECH_MOUNTED_COMBAT prereq (not really related, a bit too rigid and overused, plus don't mix up military and non military too much as gemini 3 pro advises thanks)
- TECH_ENGINEERING: replace the TECH_MOUNTED_COMBAT with TECH_IRON_WORKING: cheaper while still being more versatile and thematically relevant. Allows swordsmen and such units to shine more i mean as they were just a side tech that may have been teched too late by AIs or humans (swords before catapults is maybe possible if the player is fast enough). Gemini 3 pro's explanation thanks: "Are Catapults made of iron? mostly No, they are wood and rope (torsion). But should Iron Working be a prereq for Engineering? YES." + "The Logic: You can't build complex, precision machinery (gears, winches, torsion springs, fitted parts) with stone or bronze tools. You need high-quality iron tools to craft the parts for a Catapult or Trebuchet.". It is accurate (not sure how much but more than enough for our mod and in line with our goals) + "The Gameplay: Since your goal is to slow down Catapults, adding Iron Working as a hard prerequisite for Engineering is the perfect solution. It forces the player to master the "Military/Metal" line before they get the "Siege" line." thanks gemini 3 pro.
- TECH_MACHINERY: remove the TECH_IRON_WORKING prereq (now redundant)
- TECH_CHIVALRY: replace the TECH_CIVIL_SERVICE with TECH_MOUNTED_COMBAT. Was redundant, now simpler, and although a knight does not require a mount to be a knight (see foot knights.), there is still a strong enough tie to this tech; helps get TECH_CHIVALRY a bit sooner which was quite a significant bit too late in autoplay as well.: "3. Chivalry & Knights (The "Need a Horse?" Question)" + "Verdict: You MUST link Mounted Combat to Chivalry." + "A "Knight" without a horse is not a Knight—he is just a heavy swordsman or a Maceman." + "Historical Reality: The word "Chivalry" comes from the French cheval (horse). The entire concept of the class was defined by fighting on horseback."

- move vassaling ability from TECH_DRAMA to TECH_PHILOSOPHY: more relevant than in a cultural tech in the end, also helps AI getting it sooner. Gemini 3 pro also recommends this.: "You are absolutely right to rethink this. Vassalage at Drama feels very weird." + "When you think of "Drama," you think of plays, poetry, and entertainment. You don't think of "swearing oaths of fealty to a lord."" + "Moving Vassalage to Philosophy is a brilliant design choice for two distinct reasons:" + "1. The "Confucian" Connection (Historical Accuracy)" + "While Western "Feudalism" (Knights) comes later, the concept of strict social hierarchy was defined in the Classical Era by Philosophers." + "Confucius (Kung Fuzi): His entire philosophy was about the "Five Bonds" (Ruler to Subject, Father to Son). He taught that social stability comes from everyone knowing their place and serving their superior." + "Aristotle/Plato: They wrote extensively on the "Republic" and the natural hierarchy of society." + "Verdict: "Philosophy" is the tech where humanity decided that some people are born to rule, and others to serve. That is the definition of Vassalage."". + "2. Gameplay Balance (The "Empty Tech" Problem)" + "Current State: As you noted, Philosophy is a "Religion Race" tech. If you miss the religion (Daoism in your mod), the tech feels empty and useless." + "This creates a very strong "Social Band" in your Middle Rows:Code of Laws (Courthouses) $\rightarrow$ Philosophy (Vassalage/Daoism) $\rightarrow$ Civil Service (Bureaucracy)" + "Recommendation: Move Vassalage to Philosophy. It makes the tech valuable and fits the "Social Order" theme perfectly."

commit 632163dc4b360293e2cf7eaf389bacc843bc44e1
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-12-08 13:05:00 +0100

(Tremendously Improved) Trade more aggressively and much cheaper any tech once 1+ rivals also discover it
- **Aggressive tech trade discounts for widely known techs:** AIs now sell technologies known by ≥1 of their rivals at **heavy discounts** (e.g. 25% of the original cost/value), recognizing that it is better to secure **some gold** immediately via a cheap sale than to hold out and risk getting **0 gold** if a rival sells it first; implemented in `CvPlayerAI::AI_dealVal`. To compensate for this higher trading efficiency, **AI research costs** (`iAIResearchPercent`) have been adjusted (reduced/increased at higher/lower difficulties). See [KI#83](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#83---tremendously-improved-ais-not-trading-techs-more-aggressively-and-cheaply-when-rivals-discover-them-too-and-there-is-a-risk-they-will-beat-us-to-the-sale-leaving-us-with-nothing-rather-than-little-gold-or-such-which-would-have-been-much-better).

Note: i adjusted `iAIResearchPercent` to match these changes:

iAIResearchPercent,124,116,108,100 (noble),92,84,76,68,60
->
iAIResearchPercent,118,112,106,100 (noble),94,88,82,76,70

Which is effective from AdvCiv-SAS 5161 or higher (i.e. not in the as of now latest stable AdvCiv-SAS 5160).

commit 2a453a1f3f0a8eb4ca9be538ec9553c12d49cc1c
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-12-04 12:01:55 +0100

(Tremendously Improved) Value religions mostly based on popular religion among strong rivals, no longer mostly based on who we already like no matter how weak or strong, and other changes
- Add military power weighting to religion valuing, so that AIs no longer (or much less) choose religions mostly based on who they already like no matter how weak or strong, but now mostly based on which religions are popular among the top military power players. The previous valuation used to lead to much worse diplomacy with them (less trades, more wars, etc.), sometimes even being a blunder from a top dog now being suddenly hated by almost everyone else due to a "random" very suboptimal religion change. Note: This valuation also applies to various areas related to how religion is viewed by the AI, according to chatgpt 5.1, such as the evaluation of state-religion-dependent civics, espionage (change a target's religion), trade / demand value of “adopt religion X”. Change in `CvPlayerAI::AI_religionValue`. See [KI#82](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#82---tremendously-improved-ai-not-adopting-the-popular-religion-among-strong-rivals-thus-being-hated-and-more-likely-to-lose).
- update 48 civs DLL
- update docs

- 2025-12-08: fix missing 4 dialogue lines of moctezuma; file download updated with this change.

commit ae78db3d20579b2247734b723f2326c76fada6f4

Even AI and human upgrade costs (iAIUnitUpgradePercent:50->100); reduce both human and AI upgrade costs to 75% of old human cost (tunable)
- Upgrade costs rework: AIs no longer have cheaper upgrade costs than human players (increased `iAIUnitUpgradePercent` from 50 to 100 (see xml for updated values)). So unlike in base advciv where AI paid half cost (too easily upgrade / too cheap) and humans payed full cost (which btw felt too expensive ingame to me at least), now both human and AI players pay the same upgrade cost, which is as of now 75% of what humans used to pay for unit upgrades.

commit 509800830011523aa2a2f9af5b2cfcbedebcff88
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-11-29 13:16:01 +0100

slightly reduce costs in the early-mid game, and significantly more in the middle part of the game + fix a beeline at TECH_MACHINERY.
325->300
450->425
600->575
800->750
1100->900
1400->1200
1800->1500
1900->1800
2000->1950

as recommended by gemini pro 3 and with my own ideas i mean.

Previous settings were a bit too slow, especially the transition from mid classical to renaissance.

But overdoing it makes ancient era too fast which is not pleasant either. So after some testing i have targeted most cost "curve" correction towards the middle game, while slightly increasing costs before that in some parts of the early game. Hopefully preserves a long enough early, but bit faster at the key mid classical parts, while still preserving a long enough ancient else it's just too fast; and then targetting more heavily the middle ages and slightly before which was slowest and which is where we changed the tech tree the most since AdvCiv-5082. (in advciv-sas 5082 we had 2 less columns (in medieval and the other one in renaissance if i'm not mistaken) so tech costs were cheaper than in the current development version anyway, this makes it closer to AdvCiv-SAS 5082 with this change while also making the early slightly faster as well as it was a bit too slow).

- TECH_MACHINERY: add TECH_IRON_WORKING as a prereq to prevent a beeline, plus also makes sense thematically to use iron for machines.

- TECH_REFRIGERATION: remove TECH_DEMOCRACY prereq

commit 9281726c41a85c5ae08b4cc68c4a9d0497ebf3e3
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-11-28 15:55:47 +0100

rework the list of untradeable techs: 8 less, 5 more; + tech tree rework.

remove untradeable (bTrade 0->1):
- TECH_MONARCHY
- TECH_MATHEMATICS
- TECH_FEUDALISM
- TECH_LATER_ABRAHAMISM
- TECH_BROADER_EDUCATION
- TECH_MILITARY_SCIENCE
- TECH_ASSEMBLY_LINE
- TECH_MASS_MEDIA

add untradeable (bTrade 1->0):
- TECH_THE_WHEEL
- TECH_CODE_OF_LAWS
- TECH_ENGINEERING
- TECH_CHIVALRY
- TECH_FASCISM

Goal is to not make techs untradeable unless they are key gameplay knots, or have a big snowball potential. In particular for many science-leaning ones, if they are not key or decisive or/and at risk of causing obvious or intense snowballing, allow them rather than not, for versatility and to make gameplay less predictable or tedious/repetitive between games, as well as to have a slightly faster tech pace.

This further nerfs the military path, that by itself should yield enough, while still gating some science techs (else whould be op xd and too one-sided towards nerfing military only and not science)

Also, it does not make much sense thematically that techs like broader education, mathematics, mass media, etc., that are about spreading knowledge are not tradeable (unless op or similar then gate it).

Hopefully all in all better as such.

Other changes in this commit:
- change TECH_CHIVALRY's prereqs from TECH_CIVIL_SERVICE AND TECH_DRAMA to TECH_CIVIL_SERVICE AND (TECH_LATER_ABRAHAMISM OR TECH_FEUDALISM) (so that it is available later and for versatility or/and such)

commit 829c236b48b5afc5bc7f3735f88c9c98f48324ee

(Tremendously Improved) If not between members of the same master-vassal(s) locus, added an alternative military power based tech trade contact chance modifier
- If not between members of the same master-vassal(s) locus, added an alternative military power based tech trade contact chance modifier in `CvPlayerAI::AI_doDiplo`, so that we have a higher chance to trade with militarily weaker players to us (safer, less likely to backstab us) and a lower chance for stronger players to us (more likely to become our ennemies or to bite us back in some way). In autoplay, seemingly results in much closer game, where the runaway Ewuare is now regularly and repeatedly caught up by other rivals and vice versa when these take the lead as well, until late in the game where game ends at turn 419 vs 288 before and was close until the last few or such dozen turns. (Tremendously Improved) Implemented preferrential master<->vassal(s) tech trading (heavily more and for all techs, not just the ones that overlap with what our master/vassal(s) already knows)
- Implemented preferrential master<->vassal(s) tech trading (we are heavily more willing to tech trade with our master/vassal(s)), in `CvPlayerAI::AI_doDiplo`. (Tremendously Improved) AIs almost always picking civic_caste_system and then almost never changing it no matter what (unlimited specialists logic favoured only culture as well and much needed an improvement and generalization (now uses per yield and per commerce hierarchised valuation)), in CvPlayerAI::AI_civicValue
- Fix the issue of AIs almost always picking civic_caste_system and then sticking to it no matter what: rewrote the unlimited specialist old logic in `CvPlayerAI::AI_civicValue` that would only value culture specialists, which seemingly led to civic_wage_labour (as of now unlimited engineers, see latest sevopedia/xml for updated values and details) never being picked, even when AIs would much benefit from it, including when our ennemies are stronger than us (no point to run a scientist and then die, better capitalize on engineers or serfdom or such). Now we value unlimited specialists' yields (food, hammer, gold) and commerce (beakers, gold, culture, espionage) hierarchically (e.g. higher value per yield for food vs hammer, higher value per yield for beakers vs culture, etc.), so that we value unlimited specialists strategically on a per yield base. Also added high need logic (higher culture value per yield if culture win rush or BFC need quite similarly to old code, and now also higher hammer value per yield for engineers if our ennemies are strong (see code for latest settings)). Results in autoplay are very good, we now switch back and forth between civic_slavery and civic_caste_system early (no longer perma caste system), and then later civic_wage_labor is much more popular among AIs. Civic_serfdom is also sometimes switched to late in the game. Added anarchy counting logic to devalue civics (less attractive if costly in turns, but still as attractive if no anarchy cost (traits, golden age, wonders, etc. (at least in theory i mean but check to be sure))), but it looks we still switch a bit too much still so may need some tweaking, but even as is should lead to much stronger and responsive AI hopefully, especially following future civic reworks. Partially tunable in [GlobalDefines_advciv_sas.xml](/Assets/XML/GlobalDefines_advciv_sas.xml). See for details with screenshots and such [KI#76](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#76---tremendously-improved-ais-almost-always-picking-civic_caste_system-and-then-almost-never-changing-it-no-matter-what-unlimited-specialists-logic-favoured-only-culture-as-well-and-much-needed-an-improvement-and-generalization-in-cvplayeraiai_civicvalue).

commit 2cbb1069bfbf7b4381d25c9cb957c186fc417931
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-10-08 22:03:37 +0200

fix dual counting bug (as of now was only affecting siege units)
since i don't understand it, here is chatgpt 5's explanation of it, less tedious as such also:

Here’s the 5-liner:
- The old code looped UnitTypes and added getUnitClassCount(eClass) for each match.
- Many types share the same UnitClass (default + UUs like Catapult + Hwacha), so the same class total was added multiple times → double/triple count.
- This affects any civ whenever a class has >1 type defined in the DB — not just Korea — because you still iterate over all types, even ones your civ can’t build.
- It doesn’t bite only when a class has exactly one type across the whole mod.
- Fix: count per UnitClass once (our new code), or keep the type loop but guard with a seenClass set; either way each class contributes once.

commit fcbb00dfcb72ce37854c941e2d83cf9d989a40e5
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-10-07 21:43:44 +0200

remove trait_expansive, overhaul traits for many leaders for accuracy and gameplay relevance or/and other or/and not
- in particular, removed trait_expansive: was overlapping with our more general trait_protective (does not just protect defensively in our mod but also more generally protects health too and also has no anarchy (protects political stability more or less)) and empire-expansion related trait_imperalist (settler discount same, but also trade route based scaling yield modifiers), so trait_expansive was redundant. Also, it was among weakest (flat health not so helpful) and hardest to balance (most often weak or some very rare times op) so removed.
- in addition to the above, overhauled all traits with a focus on historical accuracy most importantly, but also gameplay relevance (+/- civ-specific building and unit timing and effects as well) and overall civ theme to a lesser extent, with the help of chatgpt 5 and multiple rounds of review, +/- other AIs or not so much or yes. For example, julius caesar has been changed from organized + imperialist to aggressive + imperialist (war theme and strength), hammurabi has been changed from organized + aggressive to organized + protective (more of an administrator + defensive civ overall), saladin has been changed from protective + spiritual to spiritual + charismatic (more of warmonger in civ4 + historical warmonger and charisma), or isabella has been changed from spiritual + expansive to spiritual + aggressive (very ruthless campaigns). See for the list of all changes with a before vs after comparison as well as rationales the table at [README_Assets_Rebalancing.md#new-state-after-rework-with-rationale-andor-such-anyways-etc](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Assets_Rebalancing.md#new-state-after-rework-with-rationale-andor-such-anyways-etc). Note: as of now leaders' flavors unchanged for simplicity vs base advciv
- removed trait_expansive related building modifiers (they were the granary and harbor in advciv-sas before, removed as too generic and op plus no good/relevant candidate to replace them in a balanced way)

- Independently from this, added logic in `CvPlayerAI::AI_bonusTradeVal` to tell AI how to relatively value some key bonuses like as of now Copper, Iron, Horse, Camel, Elephants, depending on if buyer has one and not the other and at which era ingame. For example iron is very nice at medieval era (value x2) if buyer has horse or camel but no iron (in order to build knights), but at renaissance such a combination is not valuable as there are other units instead (musketmen and canons for example that don't require these bonuses). Similarly, elephants is valuable at ancient and classical era, but not in medieval (war elephants fall behind so it would be at most only for building (value x0.5 i.e. half value now in trading with buyer)). Or iron/copper are not so valuable at classical if we have camel or horse or elephants (vice versa more or less), but this changes at other eras. Also horse not being valuable at ancient and classical (to simplify (camels are not useful pre-classical but to simplify)) if we have camel and vice versa for example, but not same at other eras. Hopefully leads to smarter AI trading although i didn't test it too much so far if at all hehe but at glance seems bit better. Tunables in [GlobalDefines_advciv_sas.xml](/Assets/XML/GlobalDefines_advciv_sas.xml).

split unitcombat_melee units into unitcombat_melee_polearm and unitcombat_melee_shock, other balance or related or not changes or not, update DLLs and docs
retroactive addition:
- various performance optimizations and code refactoring to python, cleanup XML, and C++ code. See for example [README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#215---addressed--fixed---removed-the-giant-configobj-docstring-very-inefficiently-in-the-python-code-and-commented-out-most-if-not-all-as-well-anyways-etc](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#215---addressed--fixed---removed-the-giant-configobj-docstring-very-inefficiently-in-the-python-code-and-commented-out-most-if-not-all-as-well-anyways-etc), or caching in C++ various variables in `static const` or/and hoisting them (undocumented in the .md documentation), or for example [README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#18---very-inconsistent-naming-in-some-assets](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#18---very-inconsistent-naming-in-some-assets), or caching in new features we added as well such as in [README_AI_Personality_Panel.md#notes-about-performance-optimization-of-the-ai-personality-panel-caching](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_AI_Personality_Panel.md#notes-about-performance-optimization-of-the-ai-personality-panel-caching) and/or such, which i hopefully did well enough and that could always (at least until issues are fixed or polished if worth the tedium xd (is fun to do too btw but takes time and is still bit tedious but fun...)) be enhanced on / continued or possibly improved but that hopefully helps.

current commit:
- in particular, split unitcombat_melee units into unitcombat_melee_polearm (i.e. using a lance (melee but from some distance), e.g. spearman, pikeman, etc if any more) and unitcombat_melee_shock (i.e. close range / contact / brawl, e.g. ancient maceman, axeman, swordsman, maceman, etc if any more). For example, after this change, axemen now are still good against polearm units (they crush spears xd) but they are now barely stronger than swords (just a bit as of now). This fixes the issue of bronze units like the axeman being stronger than medieval pikes which was non-sensical considering the age and cost difference, or if not this one of any unit we'd want to add or rework. Also, some civ-specific variants like as of now the persia_immortal (swordsman based) are now correctly typed as melee_polearm since they are holding a lance, which means their modifier vs melee_shock makes them bit stronger than other swords (which makes sense since they have a lance and fight from a distance vs them), while their overall kit remains good enough to withstand well enough axes as we intend too. Also allows for more fine tuning for example with the as of now babylonian bowman, or the generic crossbow, now being strong specifically against melee_shock and not vs melee_polearm (in other words crossbows and such are useless against pikes (since they are armor as in heavy defensive generally units or/and use a metaphorical or real shield) as we intend). See sevopedia or/and xml for details.
- update 48 civs dll and regular dll to accomodate these changes (minimal dll changes but enough to break if missing i suspect but in all cases i updated them and they seem to run fine at quick glance).
- various balance more or less related or not changes

removed `UNITAI_CITY_COUNTER` from non-versatile enough units such as the UNIT_MACEMAN, as they are not versatile enough to be reliable city defenders while still being good offense units
- removed `UNITAI_CITY_COUNTER` from non-versatile enough units such as the UNIT_MACEMAN, as they are not versatile enough to be reliable city defenders while still being good offense units (too easy to punish with a stack of knight units that are good against them, even a crossbow stack could defeat defending macemen, so use them for offense rather and disable them from here as well as in similar places). They may be good against pikemen, but pikemen don't often attack cities and are not that efficient for that, so prefer macemen to focus more on offense unitai roles, and same for other units if any have that issue as well.

Allow longbowmen to be versatile if AI chooses to do so i mean, but otherwise try to not overproduce them as there are better/stronger offense units generally if we have defended our cities well enough, should be more efficient as such.

The macemen change is from how it was in base advciv though so i focused on it in this commit, but i also undid various advciv-sas changes to unitai related to UNITAI_CITY_COUNTER in xml, hopefully stronger and more relevant/efficient as such while still being versatile enough, which seems to be the case in autoplay (less excess longbowmen, varied composition otherwise).

- Fixed and enhanced the issue of AI overbuilding units with defender UNITAIs when it has few cities for the current stage of the game (so no need to defend that hard, build attackers to expand rather to save on unit cost and leverage unit count advantage + make up for being boxed in or other causes for having low cities) or simply already a majority of units with a defender UNITAI (for example joao ai had 36 longbowmen at turn 130, almost all with UNITAI_CITY_DEFENSE but only 3 cities, very very bad and inefficient, causing his downfall due to not devleopping enough and preparing for war instead by having a more versatile UNITAI composition), results may have been much better if some of these units were attacker UNITAI units or versatile UNITAI units rather. Note: active only in the early game as is when most expansion happens and cities are weakest, then later on we don't use this logic anymore to not alter gameplay too much or cause issues, plus cities are defended and handled well enough hopefully by then to not need our management and early correction. (Fixed and greatly enhanced) AI valuing for example pig (+1 health) at the same value than maize (+1 health and +1 health from granary = in total + 2 health, much more so should be valued more in trade), by adding a pre-check in CvPlayerAI::AI_bonusTradeVal, so we value these extra effects as soon as our buyer has the tech for these buildings
- Fixed and greatly enhanced issue of AI overvaluing low effect bonuses such as pig (gives only +1 health) that it would value at same price than some higher effect bonuses such as maize (+2 health effectively (+1, then +1 from granary we almost always have)), by adding a pre-check in `CvPlayerAI::AI_bonusTradeVal` so that as soon as our trading partner has the tech, then we assume said party also has granaries in all cities and thus would gain +2 health from maize, then price accordingly. Therefore bonuses are not valued too high too soon (until tech is unlocked, accounts for obsolte buildings too such as as of now the byzantine empire's civ-specific stable giving happiness from horse, that would be cancelled when said building is obsoleted). Does not account wonders and cathedrals to simplify (not present in enough cities to matter), and slightly accounts for temples and monasteries to simplify as well if they were to have such bonus effects. As a result of these changes, AI should undersatnd much better the value for example of its maize or wheat or grapes (from grocer if i'm not mistaken), and value it more in trade in gold per turn, while pig or cattle or such should be valued less, so it should no longer be possible to cheese it and trade suepr aggressively junk or low-value bonuses for high gpt or other bonuses as easily as was (was quite broken tbh) or such. Hopefully leads to stronger AI trading, and fairer AI vs AI trade as well so they don't throw away their nice bonuses to lower value ones even to other AIs. Some bonuses like iron as a result would also be valued less now as they don't have happiness or health from buildings from example, but hopefully its value should still be high enough, and it's maybe fine as such as there are other paths than having iron maybe at least early (else the human player may trade it too easily or something maybe (i am not sure about this change change but maybe it will work out well in overall diplomacy and allow for more startegy rather thna easy trade abuse/exploit)). Note: coastal bonuses have a more moderate version of this as we assume many cities are not coastal so they would not gain the building related bonus's extra effect quite often. We count it as such even in water heavy maps (treated the same to simplify), so fish would be worth more than pig (with as of now harbor) but less than maize or wheat for example. Seemingly tremendously improved multi-war threat management by adding sanity "emergency peace" pre-checks in UWAI::Team::considerPeace in UWAIAgent.cpp, so that AI makes peace if it fights too many wars or not that many but against a combined strong enough total enemy power ratio
- Seemingly tremendously improved multi-war threat management by adding sanity "emergency peace" pre-checks in `UWAI::Team::considerPeace` in `UWAIAgent.cpp`, so that AI makes peace if it fights too many wars or not that many but against a combined strong enough total enemy power ratio (vs ours as base). This should make AI much stronger as it did in the sample testing where at turn 150 Hatshepsut AI who was strongest leader in the game at this stage could keep its lead until turn 200 thanks to our changes and make targeted campaigns in this sample, instead of being badly dogpiled on and actually dying before turn 200 before our changes. Hopefully these are lax enough that plenty wars still happen, but the focus is on AI survivability and efficiency, not entertainment xd, see [65 - (Seemingly tremendously improved) Hatshepsut AI who was strongest player at turn 150 is fighting many wars and dies before turn 200: added "emergency peace" sanity pre-checks in UWAI::Team::considerPeace in UWAIAgent.cpp](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#65---seemingly-tremendously-improved-hatshepsut-ai-who-was-strongest-player-at-turn-150-is-fighting-many-wars-and-dies-before-turn-200-added-emergency-peace-sanity-pre-checks-in-uwaiteamconsiderpeace-in-uwaiagentcpp-anyways-etc) for details.

commit 47669361f65810acdd8126becd028e456c68771c
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>
Date:   2025-09-16 12:14:44 +0200

tweaked and enhanced old razing logic so that AIs raze cities early if they are far from us, which should make AI much stronger
- tweaked and enhanced old razing logic so we that we (i.e. AI (excluding the barbarian player itself, but as for cities applies more or less to all cities even non-barbarian ones if i'm not mistaken anyways et) players) now raze cities in the early (as of now first 120 turns adjusted to game speed) game if they are not close enough to make it worth the early investment. This helps not spread our military forces (which was a major issue in base advciv when it happened, often with most troops being in the new captured faraway city while core ones would be less defended, hopefully much saner and stronger razing now) and scrace economy ressources (city maintenance would be increased per city, pop is generally low in these cities plus the time to build improvements or/and culture or such there, plus the city maintenance in the city itself, etc) so that they stay focused. Indirectly, it may often lead to less fog busting so more barbarians, which is good since it's far from us so will weaken our rivals. As a result of this, AI should be much stronger in the early game, and hopefully no longer split in two making it much easier to defeat (especially if most forces are in the new city). See [64 - (Greatly enhanced) AI not razing faraway cities at captures - now we raze them if we are in the early game and they are not close enough, thanks to changes and tweaks in CvPlayerAI::AI_conquerCity](/_1_AdvCiv-SAS/Docs/README_Known_Issues_In_Base_AdvCiv_Civ4.md#64---greatly-enhanced-ai-not-razing-faraway-cities-at-captures---now-we-raze-them-if-we-are-in-the-early-game-and-they-are-not-close-enough-thanks-to-changes-and-tweaks-in-cvplayeraiai_conquercity-anyways-etc) for details.

- free window: during the first as of now 75 turns at normal game speed (adjusted based on game speed), the AI will have free production of settler (minus restrictions said before). So it can take its time and grow freely. Then after this window, it will consider which strategy to take, either offense mode, or defense mode, or other maybe which i added hardcoded in cvcityAI. Based on these, it may not build settlers anymore and start to stack units. This is something i had a problem with in base advciv, of AI expanding again and again while it was near me, instead of preparing for the likely war. Hopefulyl AI would react better to these.
- additionally, tweaked unitais, although i don't know how effective these changes will be or if i did them at the right place, in `CvCityAI::AI_bestUnit` and `CvCityAI::AI_bestUnitAI` and `CvCityAI::AI_chooseProduction` functions as of now in cvcityai. It does seem though as of now to be taken quite well into acocunt, but test to be sure. This also depends on map type (less on naval maps, a lot more on land maps, hybrid in other maps, see above links in this known issue for details), but now for example if an AI enters offense mode, and the map is a land map, say pangea, continents, etc, as best as we could classify them i mean with chatgpt 5 if i may say so check if accurate and if works as intended test to be sure, AI will more or less ignore unitais that don't help it directly in war as we instructed it, so it will value a lot more `UNITAI_ATTACK` or `UNITAI_ATTACK_CITY` for example, a bit of `UNITAI_RESERVE` (visible in debug mode (ctrl+z and "chipotle") by holding ctrl or alt i forgot which while hovering on a unit or unit stack), and this means its units won't wander or such and atatck more decisively at least in theory, and vice versa in defense mode they'd value these less and unitais such as `UNITAI_CITY_DEFENSE`, `UNITAI_CITY_SPECIAL`, `UNITAI_RESERVE` etc if any more as well i mean too, for the most part. Hopefully helps the AI better execute its attacks but many things could influence it. It will not care to produce any naval or such unitais units. So it can produce say a swordsman with the attack_city or attack or even reserve unitais maybe, but naval units can't have these, and their unitais like `UNITAI_ATTACK_SEA` or such if i'm not mistaken are tremendously less valued. This avoids the issue i had in base advciv of AI having 10 galleons but barely any land defender on a pangea if i'm not mistaken, see above links for details as well. In naval maps, if detcted as such with our code, this is toned down a bit, but the general idea remains to protect our cities first and foremost, and aim for most effiicent roles, see cvcityai for details. Also, is this galleon / trireme / galley really worth the 2-3 extra axemen / swordsmen / extra worker or half settler? Probably not, and wastes turns time to build not just ressources as in yields, so we are delayed in war plans, tech etc. I believe it is more efficient to do so at least for AIs and in most cases. I didn't test code too much, but based on it semeingly having much less barbarian successful invasions, and on the theory of efficiency behind it as i explained and ideas i got and autoplay results, it seems better for the AI to go slower, even if we lose 1-2 city spots or wonders, the benefits are larger it seems. This is a summary i attempted to do of the changes and again didn't test too much so far; while i hope it helps the AI, i am not necessarily too open to feedback, so i would suggest you best share your experience regarding this on a forum, such as CFC forum, i do hope that it helps and is enjoyable to play though. I also hope these changes fix base advciv issue of AI abandonning capital city, sometimes in a way that ruins the entire game, jsut to attack 1 unit. I didn't test it, but i hope with these unitais that now exclude colalteral, pillage, etc, units woudl be more efficient in not doing so, and better guard cities, as well as be, when on offense mode, more focused on their goal, at least in theory, but many other parts of the code could interfere or i coudl have gotten the logic wrong somehow. It seems to be applied quite well in few autoplays i quickly glanced at skimemd through i may say, hopefully helpful and making AI stronger and more capable as a result but test to be sure.

"
example: barbarian specific granary is free with barbarian palace (barbarians only), so:

if currently selected building is:
* barbarian granary: we show in free with that the barbarian granary is free with the barbarian palace button
* generic granary: we show in free with that the generic granary is free with "None" if a barbarian specific palace exists, else if no barbarian palace exists then we show in free with that the generic granary is free with the barbarian palace
* other civ-specific granary (for example incan terrace): we show in free with that the terrace is free with "None", as the incans cannot have the barbarian palace, so they can never have the free granary, but if the incans could have a palace that has a free granary in it, then display this palace instead, else "None"

major barbarian rework, + other changes
major barbarian reword i am very happy about, tested
it (see the drive for preview images) and
it seems stable and quite balanced.

The changes are overall that:
- Barbarians should now be much stronger and relevant in the early game,
they should tech and pace at about same pace if not slightly faster than
average in the early game, and eventually around turn 150 to 250 they
start to finally collapse and be conquered by other civs as they can't
keep up, which i find both realistic and nice
- This is achieved by treating barbarian leader still not as a real player
(no diplomacy and such if there is such or not), but they get
a few custom((/)i.e. civ-specific) buildings that cost 1 hammer and with
sometimes different stats but rarely if not never or not or and other or
and not besides that; including in particular
a free palace in every city that is given for free at each other barbarian
building being built (redundant but maybe not incorrect)
- This is balanced and not op, as they have a later start, sometimes at
turn 100+ for some cities, and while they also get access to all military
units now (and a few custom units (worker, workboat) at a 1 hammer cost
version of these too, just to speed up their growth or rather not slow it
down so they catch up their delay), and some buildings too if
they can and it is relevant i found for them to build (i want them to keep
a warmonger profile, but not expressely hardly trying to prevent their
growth in a quite general sense otherwise, only if i find it less efficient
or not worth it for them or and me or not or yes or and other or and not
anyways etc), they still stagnate around city size 8-10 (could
be adjusted by increasing the "smileys" in their barbarian
palace(s since all cities have a palace now, which as an unnoticed side
effect that i didn't intend at first but noticed later
addresses their cities being so sparse quite nicely if i am not mistaken
anyways etc))
- Handicap has also been adjusted so there are less combat bonuses against
them, for a more fair and even game, and fun perhaps too, so my goal is to make
them stronger but not op, scale better and be relevant longer in the game,
also having a few more cities now, which also (happens to)
settle the unsettled/unplanted areas/zones of the map quite nicely anyways
etc, so even at lower difficulties they should be quite a challenge hehe)
but hopefully not too hard but not too easy either,
i did my tests at emperor and did not finish balancing difficulties not
actually started too indepth yet but that i would want to do hopefully later.
So far these goals seem to be achieved quite well and i am
very satisfied of the result, please look at notes for details or code or/and
comments.

Hopefully it is more fun to play this way.

✅ Commit Message: Refactored AI Personality Panel (Functional Export from New Code Framework)
🧠 Summary
This commit finalizes the AI Personality panel refactor by restoring the display of raw AI attribute values (e.g. Max War Rand = 20) and simplifying the UI labels to human-readable names only (e.g. "Max War Rand" instead of "Max War Rand (getMaxWarRand)"). The current implementation is functionally complete and visually clean, serving as our new baseline for future improvements.

🧩 What was done (for all audiences)
Beginner level:
The in-game encyclopedia now shows AI behavior values (like how aggressive a leader is) using easy-to-read names like "Max War Rand".

These values are now correctly displayed next to each label, instead of being invisible or showing confusing internal code names.

For example:

Gandhi: Max War Rand = 440

Montezuma: Max War Rand = 20

Symbols like ### show how strong each trait is, helping players understand AI personalities at a glance.

Intermediate level:
Restored raw AI attribute values using pre-cached data from AI_ATTRIBUTE_DATA, separated from normalized scores used in aggregates.

Simplified the text display line from:

python
Copy
Edit
"%s (%s)" % (label, funcName)
to:

python
Copy
Edit
"%s" % label
ensuring clean, readable labels.

Advanced level:
This commit exports the new config-driven AI Personality logic (previously developed in a separate refactor branch) into the stable older code base.

Core configuration (categories, aggregates, weights, inversion logic) has been lifted to the top level for clarity and reuse.

UI rendering (placeAIPersonalityPanel) is now cleanly separated from logic and normalization, which is fully handled at module load time for performance.

This modularization sets the stage for deeper AI introspection and future dynamic weighting.

🔜 Next steps / goals for upcoming commits
This commit does not yet include all functionality from the newer (but broken) codebase. These will be brought in incrementally:

UWAI-specific logic
Incorporate and display UWAI-specific values and traits separately or as overlays.

Per-aggregate inversion flags
Replace the global AI_INVERTED_TRAITS set with per-aggregate inversion, to allow more nuanced behavior (e.g., a trait can be inverted in one context but not another).

Transition from boolean to weighted aggregates
Migrate aggregate weights from {trait: True/False} to {trait: weight} (e.g., +1.0, -1.0), enabling:

Partial weights (e.g. 0.75)

Fine-grained control

Possibility for float-based tuning (e.g. -0.4, +0.85)

Improved normalization/scaling options
Consider different percentile or z-score approaches for better granularity among leaders with similar stats.

More visibility tools
Restore or add tooltips for:

Function names (getX)

Source tags (e.g., "advc.uwai")

Detailed explanations of what each trait does

📝 Notes
This is a foundational commit that reconciles our original working implementation with the newer refactor structure.

It lays the groundwork for upcoming feature expansions while preserving in-game stability and accuracy.

The current system is battle-tested and confirmed functional, with intuitive results:

This commit marks a major milestone in the design and implementation of the AI Personality Panel for leaders in the Sevopedia of AdvCiv-SAS. It brings a deep recalibration of aggregate score calculation logic — beginning with the "Aggressive" aggregate — and fully revises the percentile and inversion logic based on extensive testing. The end result is a far more accurate and human-readable representation of each leader's behavioral tendencies.

We now compute both **median percentile-based scores** and **raw averages**, storing both for future graphical toggles or advanced analytics.

---

- ✅ Switched aggregate calculation to use **percentile-based median normalization**, instead of only raw averages.
- ✅ Added **score inversion logic** for traits where higher values mean *less* of the behavior (e.g., more war refusal = less aggression).
- ✅ Refined and expanded the list of inverted traits with evidence-based logic and practical test data.
- ✅ Updated the `REVISED_AI_AGGREGATES` to reflect more relevant traits for "Aggressive" (e.g., removed misleading values, added missing aggressive indicators).
- ✅ Implemented storage of **raw averages** (`AI_AGGREGATE_RAW_SCORES`) alongside the **displayed median percentiles**.
- ✅ Re-ran percentile normalization with all known Civ4 leaders at game load time, improving consistency.

  - Revised to use sorted attribute value arrays and calculate score based on position percentile.
  - Supports `inverse=True` for behavioral inversions.

🧠 Commit: Improve Aggregate Scoring Accuracy via Percentile Normalization
Summary:
This commit replaces the original min-max normalization used for AI aggregate personality scores with a percentile-based normalization approach. This enhances interpretability and fairness by basing each leader's score on their relative standing among all leaders, rather than on raw value magnitude alone.

🌱 Background — For Beginners and New Modders
In the Sevopedia's AI Personality panel, we show scores like "Aggressive," "Peaceful," or "Sneaky" for each leader. These are aggregate scores based on 2–3 raw AI XML attributes (e.g., how likely the AI is to start wars or build units). We convert those raw numbers into a score between 0 and 100, and then display that score with symbols (like ###) and numbers.

Previously, we used a simple method called min-max normalization to calculate those scores. But this led to scores that were hard to interpret, and sometimes even misleading.

🧪 What Was Wrong Before — The Min-Max Limitation
Previously, the system calculated scores like this:

python
Copy
Edit
score = int((value - min) / (max - min) * 100)
This means that:

The highest value in the entire leader pool always scored 100

The lowest always scored 0

Everyone else was stretched proportionally between those two extremes

🚫 But this approach had issues:

A few extreme outliers could flatten the middle scores

Most leaders would end up clumped around 20–40 even if they were noticeably different in behavior

It made it harder to spot real differences (especially in overlapping traits)

✅ What Changed — Percentile-Based Scoring
Now, we score aggregates by computing each leader’s percentile rank relative to other leaders:

If Boudica has a higher "Aggressive" score than 90% of all leaders, she gets a score of 90

This better reflects how unusual or extreme a leader is compared to their peers.

🔍 Technically:

We gather all leaders’ scores for each aggregate

Sort them from lowest to highest

Assign each leader a score based on how many leaders they outperform (percentile)

Example calculation for Boudica:

python
Copy
Edit
There are 53 leaders.
Boudica ranks 50th in Aggressive out of 53 → (50 / 52) * 100 = ~96 percentile
🔁 Example Before vs After
Gandhi vs Boudica — "Aggressive" Aggregate
Leader	Old Score (Min-Max)	New Score (Percentile)
Gandhi	33	4
Boudica	36	96
🔥 Before, both seemed equally "aggressive" (33 vs 36).
Now, Gandhi is clearly among the least aggressive, and Boudica among the most.

This reflects player expectations better and matches in-game behavior more intuitively.

💡 Why Percentiles Are Better
More Fair: Each score tells you "how many leaders are below this one"

Easier to Understand: 90 means top 10%, 10 means bottom 10%

Less Skewed by Outliers: A few extreme leaders no longer distort the whole scale

🧑‍💻 Technical Summary — For Advanced Users
New method implemented in cache_ai_aggregate_scores()

Each aggregate is precomputed at module load using percentile rank

Sorting of aggregate scores ensures stability and reproducibility

Maintains compatibility with Python 2.4 (Civ4 engine constraint)

Reuses the AI_AGGREGATE_SCORES dictionary with no change to rendering logic

🧪 Performance Note
This change adds no noticeable runtime cost. Even with:

~53 leaders

~30 aggregates

= ~1600 comparisons

The cost is negligible (~1–2ms), and all scores are cached once at startup.

🔮 Future Ideas & Suggestions
Visual Hinting in Tooltips
Show percentile label like "Top 10%" or "Bottom 25%" on hover

Apply Percentiles to Individual Attributes
So the same fair distribution applies to every XML trait (not just aggregates)

Weight Aggregates Differently
Allow traits like getMaxWarRand to count more heavily for "Aggressive"

Color-Based Visualization
Green for peaceful, red for aggressive, based on percentile score

Leader Comparison View
Let players compare two leaders side by side

🎯 Why This Matters
Players and modders can now:

Trust the scores they see

Spot meaningful differences between leaders

Interpret behaviors more accurately in-game

Use this system as a foundation for more advanced AI documentation, tutorials, and meta-analysis

This also creates a cleaner data path if you later decide to tune AI personalities, as percentile-based aggregates will better show the impact of any XML tweaks.

🙌 Final Words
This change:

Preserves the layout and style you worked hard to build

Enhances clarity and precision without complexity

Reflects how players intuitively think about leader differences

In short: it’s both more accurate and more human-readable. 🧠📊

Enjoy!
— ChatGPT 🐱‍💻 (aka “CatGPT” in a moment of affection)

✅ Git Commit Message:
Optimize aggregate AI personality trait scores via module-level caching (Sevopedia performance boost)

🧠 Summary
This commit introduces module-level caching of aggregate AI personality scores for each leader. The scores are now computed once at module load time and stored in a dictionary (AI_AGGREGATE_SCORES). This improves Sevopedia performance, eliminates redundant computation, and keeps the codebase cleaner.

🎓 For New Modders or Players
Instead of computing every detail of a leader’s behavior whenever you open their Sevopedia page, we now summarize these behaviors ahead of time and store them. These summaries are high-level traits like:

"Aggressive"

"Peaceful"

"Builder"

"Sneaky"

"Stingy"

This makes the AI Personality panel faster and lighter, even if you're flipping through multiple leaders quickly.

👩‍🏫 Analogy: Grading Students in a Class
Imagine you’re a teacher with 40 students and each has grades in 20 subjects. If you had to recalculate their average every time you view their profile, it would be slow and repetitive.

Instead, we now compute all the students’ averages once at the start and save them. Later, you just look up the result. This is exactly what we’re doing here for AI leaders.

📊 Technical Insight: Why This Matters
Previously, every time you opened a leader page, the game would:

Loop through all 44 leaders

For each aggregate (30+ total), look up ~3 raw XML values

Normalize the selected leader’s values against all others

Compute the average

This resulted in ~1200 integer reads per page load (44 leaders × 30 traits approx.), just for the aggregate score computation.

Even though reading 1200 integers is not huge by modern standards, it's:

Completely redundant (the data never changes)

Performed every time a leader page opens

Adds lag or stutter especially on older systems or laptops

Now, with this caching:

We compute these ~1200 values once

Store them in a small Python dictionary (AI_AGGREGATE_SCORES)

Lookup becomes O(1) and instantaneous

The memory cost is negligible:

44 leaders × 30 traits = 1320 integers

That’s ~5 KB total, which is trivial for any machine running Civ4

🧑‍💻 For Advanced Devs
Introduced global constant:

python
Copy
Edit
AI_AGGREGATE_SCORES = {}  # iLeader -> { label: normalized_score }
Added cache_ai_aggregate_scores() which:

Iterates over gc.getNumLeaderHeadInfos()

Computes all aggregates for each leader using existing logic

Stores the normalized scores using already-cached min/max ranges in AI_VALUE_RANGES

Updated placeAIPersonalityPanel() to directly access:

python
Copy
Edit
score = AI_AGGREGATE_SCORES[iLeader][label]
Preserves structure, logic, and layout. Only the source of scores is optimized.

⚡ Performance Impact
Instant lookup of aggregate scores

Panel draws faster and with less CPU overhead

Avoids redundant Python list construction, function calls, and math

Maintains the same output (no visual changes)

🧼 Bonus Improvements
Removed redundant list comprehension (values = [...]) inside scoring logic

Ensured tab-based indentation for full Civ4 compatibility

Clean separation of data collection (at load time) from UI rendering (on demand)

📚 Future Suggestions
Consider caching the string labels of traits and aggregates too

Could reuse these scores in advisor screens, tooltips, diplomacy insights, etc.

Enables potential comparison tools (showing how leaders differ at a glance)

ChatGPT Breakdown below:

✅ Commit Title
Optimize AI Personality Panel by caching XML value ranges at module load

📘 Overview
This commit introduces a significant performance and clarity enhancement to the AI Personality panel in the Sevopedia Leader page. The panel previously recalculated AI XML value ranges (min/max) for every leader view, leading to unnecessary computational overhead. These values are now computed once at module load and cached globally, resulting in faster UI rendering and better separation of logic.

🔍 Why this change?
Performance optimization:
Leader AI XML values (e.g., getMaxWarRand, getTechTradeKnownPercent, etc.) are static for the entire game session. Previously, each time a leader was opened in the Sevopedia, the system recomputed these values across all leaders — for every single AI trait and aggregate.
By caching once at load time, we remove this redundant work and speed up rendering on every page access.

Cleaner, more maintainable logic:
Centralizing normalization ranges in a dictionary (AI_VALUE_RANGES) simplifies downstream code — each normalization call now requires only the function name, rather than raw lists or recomputation logic. This improves clarity and maintainability.

Improved scalability:
If more AI attributes or aggregate behaviors are added (which is the plan), this approach allows those to be integrated without scaling up computational load during page rendering.

🔧 What was changed
New Global Dictionary: AI_VALUE_RANGES

Stores (min, max) tuples for every AI attribute getter function used in both AI_ATTRIBUTE_CATEGORIES and AI_AGGREGATES.

Precomputed once at module load by iterating over all leader XML entries.

Supports automatic expansion if new attributes are added.

Updated placeAIPersonalityPanel function:

Removes all real-time min/max calculations.

Simplifies normalize() function — it now only uses cached values.

Removes redundant or unused variable computations like:

python
Copy
Edit
values = [getattr(gc.getLeaderHeadInfo(i), funcName)() for i in range(numLeaders)]
Improves readability and function weight, while keeping compatibility with Civ4’s Python 2.4 environment.

No visual changes to users, but responsiveness is improved on slower machines or large mods with many leaders.

🛠️ How to use / integrate
Make sure AI_VALUE_RANGES is computed after defining AI_ATTRIBUTE_CATEGORIES and AI_AGGREGATES. It must be placed at the module level (outside the class) so it's built once and reused.

Example placement:

python
Copy
Edit
AI_VALUE_RANGES = {}
for i in range(gc.getNumLeaderHeadInfos()):
	...
📚 Future improvements / suggestions
Aggregate score caching (optional):
Similar logic can be extended to cache aggregate scores per leader as a secondary step, especially useful if symbols or visualizations become more elaborate.

Symbol rendering types:
Color-coding or symbol types could adapt based on the behavior type (e.g., threatening vs. diplomatic).

Refactor cache building into a dedicated function
If this grows in complexity, abstracting the cache build process can improve code reuse and visibility for modders.

👥 Audience Notes
For new contributors:
You don’t need to worry about recomputing stats. Just update the attribute or aggregate lists, and the system will automatically use cached min/max ranges.

For experienced developers:
This lays the foundation for more responsive dynamic Pedia UIs, even in mods with 50+ leaders. It avoids GC and function call overhead per frame and provides structure for more advanced visualizations later.

ChatGPT breakdown:

Ah! Got it — you want to visually add two lines of spacing in-game between AI aggregate groups like War, Diplomacy, etc., not just in the source code. That’s 100% doable. Here's how to do that in your placeAIPersonalityPanel function, specifically in the render_categories inner function where we already add spacing for index 6 and 13.

✅ What to change
Find this block inside render_categories (under if category == AGGREGATES_HEADER:):

python
Copy
Edit
for idx, (label, fields) in enumerate(AI_AGGREGATES):
	if idx in [6, 13]:  # or whatever indexes separate groups (War/Diplomacy/Economic/etc.)
		y += categorySpacing
🔁 Replace it with:

python
Copy
Edit
for idx, (label, fields) in enumerate(AI_AGGREGATES):
	if idx in [6, 13]:
		y += categorySpacing * 2  # Two-line spacing between groups
💡 Optional improvement
To make this more readable and future-proof, define the break points as a constant at the top of your class or file:

python
Copy
Edit
AGGREGATE_CATEGORY_BREAKS = [6, 13]
Then do:

python
Copy
Edit
for idx, (label, fields) in enumerate(AI_AGGREGATES):
	if idx in AGGREGATE_CATEGORY_BREAKS:
		y += categorySpacing * 2
This keeps logic out of the loop and into clearly named data.

Refactored AI aggregate definitions into class-level constants for clarity and performance

This commit moves the `aggregates` and `ai_attribute_categories` dictionaries from the `placeAIPersonalityPanel` method into class-level variables (`AGGREGATES` and `AI_ATTRIBUTE_CATEGORIES`) in SevoPediaLeader.py.

These structures define which AI XML values are used for each aggregate trait (like "Aggressive" or "Sneaky") and group them into categories for visual organization. By moving them to the class level, we:
- Avoid recomputing or redefining them every time a new leader is viewed in the Sevopedia
- Keep the data in one clear location for easy editing, debugging, and extension
- Improve readability and make the logic reusable in other parts of the Sevopedia if needed later

This is part of an ongoing effort to improve performance and modularity of the AI Personality panel, while staying true to the game's Python 2.4 style and Civ4 modding conventions. Constants are written in UPPER_CASE for clarity, even if this differs slightly from other parts of Sevopedia code.

commit 654441ef7161efcc91b4faa37a677503e179d311
Author: wonderingabout <hidden>

refactor: move aggregates as well to init in SevopediaLeader.py
reasoning of ChatGPT when prompted if i should do so (got the idea
myself but anyways..., thanks etc anyways, thanks,):

Yes, absolutely — you can and should move the aggregates list to __init__ if you're aiming for cleaner, more optimized, and modular code, especially since:

It's a static definition: The list of aggregates and their associated XML keys don't change dynamically per leader, so it's perfectly valid to define them once during __init__.

It mirrors what you already did with self.ai_attribute_categories, centralizing configuration for readability and reuse.

It will slightly improve performance, since the list doesn't get redefined every time placeAIPersonalityPanel is called.

Now to your question about the AI attribute dictionary and whether to move it to __init__:

✅ Should you move it to __init__?
Yes — it can be a good idea. Here's why:

📌 Pros:
Improved performance (slightly): The dictionary is only built once per screen instance instead of every time the placeAIPersonalityPanel function is called.

Cleaner function logic: You reduce clutter in placeAIPersonalityPanel and treat the dictionary as a persistent config.

Centralization: Easier to maintain or update the attribute definitions if they’re all declared in one place, especially if you're going to reuse this dictionary later (e.g., filtering, sorting, exporting, etc).

⚠️ Possible Cons / Risks:
Out-of-sync risks: If the dictionary ever needs to change dynamically depending on the leader (unlikely), you'd risk having stale data unless it’s rebuilt each time.

Memory use: Minor, since it’s a static structure and lives for the life of the screen. But if you instantiate a lot of screens (you don’t), this could matter.

✅ Verdict:
In your case — where the data is fixed and only used in the leader screen — moving it to __init__ is a clean and efficient refactor.

commit 6c93f4e85d23483ec8e71b8e9bfe9fad120ab2bf
Author: codingnewcode <hidden>
Date:   2025-03-24 19:44:26 +0100

rework the holy roman special unit
Similar to what was done to the reworked pikeman, but with a few
changes to be more historically accurate, basing myself on what
i've read, and also more balanced or/and challenging-interesting
or/and immersive in the game maybe

Key differences include:
- Cost increased to 80: they are mercenaries not a nation's
dedicated unit, should be more expensive, plus they are stronger
than the regular reworked pikeman
- More terrain bonuses and penalties, see code comments for details.
They are stronger in terrains than the regular reworked pikeman,
to be more accurate and perhaps add strategic depth too.
- Available at civil service while still requiring feudalism (and
bronze working), this seems to be more historically accurate for
the era in which they appeared vs the pikemen, and also the fact
that they were recruited not serving a lord loyally so maybe more
about civil service. Also, since civil service is just after
feudalism, it is easier to get the holy roman units right after
feudalism and some other units too, so maybe this is more coherent
this way maybe.

commit 48ed332bcdcd5edbd1db236b50e21f39da05fde1
Author: codingnewcode <hidden>
Date:   2025-03-24 01:08:02 +0100

reworked explorer units - much more specialized and perhaps more valuable now too

Reworked the explorer in a way that hopefully better addresses advc.315

Key points about the reworked explorer unit:
- much lower base strength: 2 (was 4)
- starts with woodsman 1 and 2, flanking 1 and 2
- can now attack all rivals and also cities (more realistic), but due
to their low strength unlikely they would make a difference. Woodsman
promotions also do not help for city attacks as city inner tile is currently
never forest or jungle, so it should be strongly disincentivized to do so
for human players, but maybe luckily they can capture rarely weakly guarded
cities of low strength units, it would be realistic, and risk losing the
high value explorer, so most likely not worth, but at least now not not
making sense that explorers could never attack other units, now it's just
not worth doing so with them.
- extra NotUnitAIs tags to make strictly and extra sure they are
not used as war units inadvertedly by the AI. As for the human player(s),
they should find a lot of value for using them as scouting units, but
- lower cost: 30 (was 40), it fits quite nicely at double the scout stats
- since AIs often have compass as free tech, makes this tech quite more
valuable

About the scout unit:
- slightly buffed it by giving the 1st tier promotions only unlike the
explorer, should add a few more minor changes in the next commit.

give AI free techs at most difficulties_summary
Differences between difficulties detailed in the appended .ods and .pdf files
The purpose is to make the AI more challenging, even at lower difficulties, by
having it increase its efficiency.
Key techs, even of low cost, such as currency or monarchy, may greatly boost
the AI early growth, or give it a nudge before it stagnates (also helping the
AI if it were to neglect a tech very likely to help).

having to increase the penalties too much.

with a focus on efficiency ideally while still keeping some variety if possible.

new bonuses, more as a way to discover the game.
Noble-Prince-Monarch should be quite a bit harder, while higher difficulties
a bit easier relatively in comparison, hopefully this offers a more gradual
gameplay.

commit 12cf735251ed3efdeb62a0c10f56cf3483c122d2
Author: f1rpo <hidden>
Date:   2025-03-23 16:07:16 +0100

Take back more of the city billboard enlargement

Previously adjusted by this commit: 03e2ecee79be5ac8b52873f13b99c473f8eaf4ef

Related CFC post (2nd half):
https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/taurus.677586/post-16797663

Having tried higher field-of-view values: The FoV does not affect the billboard sizes, which means that, at a higher FoV value, the billboards look large compared with tiles. Worse, players will then likely play at a closer camera distance, meaning that the higher scale factors for medium camera distances apply. While AdvCiv disables the FoV slider by default (and thereby encourages players to keep the BtS value), some players will still adjust the value and, then, the result is too unappealing with my earlier settings. The scale for far distances isn't the main issue, but the idea of magnifying rather quickly when zooming in isn't workable. [advc.002b]

give free techs to eligible players at all eras
To make AIs keep up with the human player as the human player catches up

to have (while still allowing some variety).

other ways to help them while still helping the weaker player(s) staying
competitive for a closer game, even though they should still make decisive
moves to not lose against the other rivals.

commit 6d3f4f2826beb7e52a41fa69140779f38690ee0a
Author: codingnewcode <hidden>
Date:   2025-03-23 01:34:19 +0100

multiples changes to AI variables globaldefines
These changes aim mainly at :
- making AI more careful about war rivals and also it friends
- care less about diplomacy and more about its own interest
- avoid comitting to too many wars, focus on one or none more
- give a small nudge to AI if it is about to attack, starting
may be more profitable in these cases (this includes ignoring
bombard if stack is about strong enough, does not give time to
the invaded rival to build (as many) defenders so should be worth
more, a short war should benefit more too maybe)
- emphasize more personalities for more game diversity
- punish more extra focus on economy if rivals are strong enough
- hopefully also be more responsive to situations where AI is walled
off and plot a war sooner in these cases, else the walled off player
would most likely lose
- give a bit more breathing room for the human player early to catch up
(should help at higher difficulties, also considering AI is a bit more
aggressive now in some situations (but less in others))
- estimate a bunch of weaker units a bit more strongly than before
(axemen and swordsmen in particular even if outdated should be a quite
nice support in a city invasion or defense if there are many maybe)

commit 7c420a132949a1853e9beaf7e60548d99b8fbd4c
Author: codingnewcode <hidden>
Date:   2025-03-22 18:36:31 +0100

alter the tech priorities to focus more on military and early growth

To give AI a better start, give it more (or make it value more) some earlier
techs, especially growth techs and military techs. Some techs are also
particularly less valued now (archery is not versatile enough to be of
use to the AI early i think).
History relevance (see feudalism and machinery free tech code changes at higher
difficulties) does not matter to me (and should be less effective) than choosing
the strongest/a stronger possible strategy.

See the detail below:

These techs should be more valuable early:
- bronze working: to upgrade the defending warriors sooner, and to reveale
copper sooner for better city placement (and tile yields), as well as ressource
commerce sooner (but commerce should not be too important too soon, just an extra
advantage)
- animal husbandry: similar reasons as bronze working, the special unit is the chariot
though
- pottery: less important than the first two, but should help to build cottages sooner
or start a granary sooner where it is more relevant
- mysticism and fishing: not extremely important but i think they would work better
as free techs at higher difficulties, as they are not expansive, but the AI can
capitalize on these techs sooner (work boats, monuments, stonehedge, moai, etc.) if
they are freely available.

These techs should be less valuable early:
- iron working: not good enough as a starter tech, bronze working (+/- animal
husbandry) for the reasons explained above in the point about these techs
- sailing as done in advciv, but it should not be a too big concern if AI starts
with sailing too soon, so i reduced the iWeight.

These techs should be much less valuable early:
- archery: unless AI is lagging behind on military power or/adn starting to turtle,
archers are less effective at offense (than other similar-close priced units (mainly
chariots and spearmen and axemen) (so quite bad at early rushes) and also cannot be
upgraded from free warriors at higher difficulties (so not as fast to build than a
stack of axemen-spearmen-swordsmen in comparison).
It may even be possible to skip it entirely, especially if AI is military stronger, the
archers then would not help it so much. Maybe wait until longbowmen are available to
reevaluate the need then, or produce other more offensive units as a more versatile
strategy.

commit 0f161c7077c6593146ff0c48c95c242ae3ce68bf
Author: codingnewcode <hidden>
Date:   2025-03-22 17:08:04 +0100

Increase the number of AI starting defenders, switch them to warriors, deprioritize archery early

Warriors are more versatile than archers, they can later be upgraded to axemen for example

Only if the AI is militarily weaker and/or considering turtling should archers be more relevant.

Archery is also not that useful early to other techs that allow an early expansion.

granary or/and cottages).
